RDA of Val Samples

MPG

8/26/2020

Input data are all samples with >20 sequences. I excluded samples from pool#5? (detailed samples). Perform RDA, inference on VAR explained, individual variable significance, and simple plot (can be done nicer to match your manuscript style)

library (readr)
## Warning: package 'readr' was built under R version 3.5.3
enviro<-read_csv(url("https://raw.githubusercontent.com/mpstroud/ValData/master/enviro.csv"))
## Parsed with column specification:
## cols(
##   Sample_Name = col_character(),
##   D10 = col_double(),
##   D50 = col_double(),
##   D90 = col_double(),
##   Org_content = col_double(),
##   FlowVel = col_double(),
##   Temp_Var = col_double(),
##   Temp_Max = col_double(),
##   Temp_Min = col_double(),
##   Temp_Mean = col_double(),
##   Max_Depth = col_double(),
##   Stdev_Depth = col_double()
## )
species<-read_csv(url("https://raw.githubusercontent.com/mpstroud/ValData/master/species.csv"))
## Parsed with column specification:
## cols(
##   .default = col_double()
## )
## See spec(...) for full column specifications.
enviro <- as.data.frame(enviro) ; rownames(enviro) <- paste(enviro$Sample_Name) ; enviro <- enviro[,2:12 ]
#will log transform environmental data to deal with units variation and associated variance.
enviro=log(enviro+1) #+1 is to get around log(negative)

#we are good to go in terms of data

I’ll use the Vegan package functions, very common and powerful

library(vegan)
## Warning: package 'vegan' was built under R version 3.5.3
## Loading required package: permute
## Warning: package 'permute' was built under R version 3.5.1
## Loading required package: lattice
## This is vegan 2.5-6
library(ggplot2)

#let's begin with a full RDA model:
rda1 <- rda(species ~ ., enviro)  # Model with all explanatory variables
rda1

#Inertia is variation, the 'constrained part' of it is the proportion of total variance in species data explained by environmental variables = 76% (pretty good)
anova(rda1) #this is to test the overall significance of the model It is p-value = 0.032

#only the D150 and D90 seem to have significant coefficients (slopes).

#Another issue is to assess what would be the most parsinomous RDA model. This is done based on R2 and P-value
rda0 <- rda(species ~ 1, enviro)  # first we run a model with intercept only, no environemtnal variables (null model) 
step.res <- ordiR2step(rda0, scope = formula(rda1), direction="both") #now we do a stepwise process to find out the "best" model (lowest AIC)
